The Samsung Galaxy S23 Ultra is a premium smartphone that offers a sleek design and impressive features, including enhanced durability. With its toughened glass front and back, aluminum frame, and IP68 dust and water resistance rating, this phone is built to withstand the rigors of everyday use.  To ensure its durability, the Galaxy S23 Ultra has undergone a series of durability tests, including drop tests and scratch tests. The device features an armor aluminum frame that provides added protection against drops and scratches, as well as a Gorilla Glass Victus 2 front and back that are designed to resist scratches and cracks.  In addition, the Samsung Galaxy S23 Ultra features an IP68 rating for dust and water resistance, making it capable of withstanding submersion in up to 1.5 meters of water for up to 30 minutes. This means you can use your phone confidently in all types of weather conditions, without worrying about damage from dust, rain, or accidental spills.  To enhance its functionality, the Galaxy S23 Ultra also comes with a stylus that features Bluetooth integration, an accelerometer, and a gyro sensor. This makes it easy to take notes, draw, and navigate the phone's interface with precision and accuracy.  Overall, the Samsung Galaxy S23 Ultra is a durable and reliable smartphone that is built to withstand the challenges of everyday life. As every client of yours is so addicted to your phones that they get them every year. Yea if only that ware true. Even your polls show that 3-4 years is the norm for a new phone and in that time a charging brick is done. So you need a charger. It uses more power, even with the magnet alignment. And multiply that by 3-4 or even 5 Billion devices, the number is quite scary. Pretty Eco friendly design. Also the materials to implement that type of charging in the phone and chargers as well, are using more resources and this is not Eco friendly. Also generating more heat because of the induction. Yea - that is one of the reasons why it's not fast, as if it was it might degrade the battery or even light it on fire.  Fourth - reparability. This is the most Eco Friendly of them all. - Make the phone as much non repairable as possible. Battery replacement, screen replacement, camera, you name it. That will save the planet. Fifth - make the new software more demanding on the phone thus pretty much requiring a new phone every couple of years as the old one will be a bit slower with every update. "Innovation" is highly subjective... personally I feel that optimization and better internals are just as innovative, if not more.  A new design is simply a new design and not innovative at all in my opinion.  Foldables are for sure innovative but I don't believe they're at the right point yet (at least for me).  So when we throw out the term innovation, I think it needs to be contextualized... what exactly are we wanting for this claim?  New materials, new shape, button-less, hidden cameras?  All of those are aesthetic and mean nothing if the internals are compromised to support them.  There's only so much you can do with the current form factor of smartphones (including foldables).  Perhaps the next innovation that would be considered as much by the majority of users would have to be a transparent phone.  :)
